Here's my analysis of 4's trailer.       MoM seems to be talking about how even though Sora saved all of his friends, if he's sad that he died he could try to return, but nothing would be the same.  We see lots of the Quadratum language. There was a 7 and 13, probably referencing, the lights and darknesses, so most of it is probably lore relevant. The full alphabet has not yet been translated sadly.  Darkside seems to be forming by using Darkness around him, maybe it's created by the negative emotions of the people.  The forest could be Endor, but nothing's really pointing to that besides it being a forest. Lots of people point out what could be an AT-ST foot, but it doesn't have the parts that stick out of one.  Sora's overall look should be the same, but he most likely only looks super realistic because of the World he's in. Almost every world gives Sora a new look, and while his overall proportions and hair are the same, his theme changes to fit the World. This world is practically identical to real life Shibuya, so he looks insanely realistic.  Strelitzia explains that this world is essentially like the afterlife, at least for her and Sora. That explains how she's here even though she died in Union X. Also, her hairclip has the roman numerals for 11 (iirc). I wouldn't be surprised if this was secretly important.  There are 2 building logos that are D-Eater and D-Dream, clearly referencing Dreams and Dream Eaters.   Darkside awakening takes place at least a little after Sora meets Strelitzia, since Sora now has his shoes on. Maybe they were going on a walk around the city. He seems unsure as to whether or not he can summon his Keyblade, so maybe Strelitzia cannot.  The "gameplay" seems mostly scripted. The UI has "Build", and Sora's grappling hook is coming from his Keyblade's keychain.  The MoM is with someone else, maybe it's Luxu.

This is a rant for the people who are less happy or generally anxious over all this potential "change" being thrown around right now.   I don't entirely get how anyone could take this as negatively as some seemingly are. Some worry I completely understand but good lord It's a single trailer and we don't even know the gameplay like--   And do people forget KH is born from taking massive risk? The original concept was FF + Disney and everyone thought that was insane then... Would SW really be THAT big of a stretch with how far we've come? And as Nomura made more games the FF character tie ins slowly faded out more and got almost entirely replaced by Nomura's characters which is... Fine even if it hurts me still because I felt like the FF characters had character development/importance with Sora and I don't understand how we didn't go to Radiant Garden in KH3 but I'm gonna go off rails so far if I don't stop there.  I can't predict what's going on behind the scenes or how much Disney properties and adventure to other worlds will be involved here because It's one freakin trailer and I'm not a wizard, But I can at least TRY off of my thoughts and feelings alone.     Compare Yozora to Sora in terms of what where and how they fight. It's quite literally like night and day and I think that's important to look at because Yozora is being represented as Sora's "other" like many characters have before except THIS time it's like a mirror of someone who is a true protagonist of their world like Sora that, in essence, Is a Final Fantasy character. And It's not like Sora isn't and hasn't been serious before... But, and this is just a hunch, I believe that Yozora has dealt with much more evil and serious problems over the course of his life.  I believe that this mysterious world Sora is in represents the SQUARE ENIX side of things being more involved this time and Nomura's strengths will shine brighter as a result, As the world may be used to put things into more of a balance like Radiant Garden once did and will help reflect how Sora has grown up further as a bonus. This doesn't have to mean Sora/Riku always have to be in the serious world and I don't think we should panic over the mere IDEA of Star Wars being in the game without even having an inkling of what's going on from one trailer (Though I'd be lying if I said that mere idea wasn't thought over in my head logistically and didn't quite make sense [Equips megaphone] *WHEN APPLYING IT TO THE USUAL FORMULA* )   No matter what it's gonna be a chaotic mess because that's how Nomura rolls in almost every thing he's written and helped write. At worst the characters development won't make sense/will contradict itself (Riku) while he simultaneously throws insane vague and or confusing plot devices (Lest we forget we long since passed the time travel line) and Nomura will add things to the plot that feel like they show up out of nowhere for the sake of sparking fresh and new feeling conflict (Insert RPG enemy group here).   Ever since Yozora started presenting himself like the original Noctis did in the old version of FF15 (Like in the car) I took it as a signal that Nomura was about to go wild. And since as people we have very different ideas you probably won't reach anywhere near having the same conclusions as me to feel more at ease and we BOTH know after coming this far there's no truly stopping even if you try to tell yourself there is (358/2 remakes and games across every console imaginable) I can at the very least tell you to just...   Buckle up.

I ain't putting up with implications of the interactions with the isolated worlds having been done an infinite amount of times...if Aqua, Terra and Ven met cinderella during the events of her movie, then Cinderella will be 10 yrs older during the events of KHI. I guess i could incorporate ideas from the live action movies like why certain disney villains turned to the darkside, thus leading up to the animated movie events... But i don't know if i should save that for backstories involving the implied Disney Verse Keyblade wielders and mentors or not. Though then again the destruction of Daybreak Town could have spread to a number of other keyblade schools or masters thus forcing them to seal their powers away by severing the connections between worlds thus creating each world's respective hearts. Like let's say Pedro Madrigal from encanto was a wielder and he sealed away his home from the encroaching darkness at the cost of his life thus creating the candle which acts as the heart of the freshly severed world of the Encanto. And wow am i getting sidetracked. But Seriously people if you dont get Kingdom Hearts worldbuilding vibes from the events in Encanto, i would be shocked.  My point is lets see what KHIV has in store and will it help enhance the ideas and changes that could help bring the KH series to life with more consistant lore, or if we should just scrap any idea of having Huey, Dewey, Louie, and Max being Sora's world traveling companions throughout the series? so we have a gachalife kh adventure, a mobile only 3d game that will most likely kill any and all battery functionality, and a game where the cartoonish look of the past installments is thrown away (aside from Donald & Goofy).  I know everyone and their grandmother is excited for another installment to Kingdom Hearts, but if this is what they're bringing to the table, they clearly didn't work hard enough.  The Disney cartoonish style was what made the first 3 games so endearing (no I'm not lumping KH3 into that mess.  I'm going story canon, so KH 1, CoM (not RE:CoM), and KH 2).  KH 3 started to deal away with the cartoonish style in favor of more cartoonish attacks, like they did in 3D.  This, along with the story falling apart, made me *LOSE* my faith in the KH Franchise after KH2.  The only one that's sort of kept the same aesthetic and storytelling was BBS and that is considered Prequel to KH1 as it's what gives Sora & Riku the ability to summon their own Keyblades.  I know from personal history that graphics do not a game make.  It's 2022 and people in their younger ages (25 and below) still enjoy Pac-Man, Pong, Galaga, and other classic titles from the 1980s and before.  Heck, even Mario Maker has the original NES style that people still love and adore to this day, and it's been almost 30 years since release (1985).  It can make a game look more pleasing to the eye, but when your previous installments heavily lent on a cartoonish style, and you're going to transfer to more realistic graphics, you should do it gradually, or make an entirely new series altogether.  Sony, if you listen to YT comments, my hope for your future installments is that you realize that graphics do not a game make, and go back to that Disney cartoonish style from the first three games (again, not lumping KH3 into that).  You can futz around with the story all you like, since we're already dealing with time travel thanks to the ending of KH3...  But messing around with graphics just because it makes it look better immediately detracts me from purchasing it.  Matter of fact, I'd rather play KH1, CoM, and KH2 again than any other installment into the franchise at this point, including the 3 mentioned in this video.  Now, I'm not saying that what they're doing is bad by any stretch.  TO ME it's a bad idea, but I'm just a normal consumer and not one of the developers or someone in the corporate ladder.  What I am, though, is an investment.  They are investing time, money, and effort, into making something that the populace will purchase and enjoy.  If the populace does not buy, then they attempt to fix what they did wrong.  What I'm trying to do is to have them dedicate more time to things that actually matter to the series canon, instead of just making it slightly more aesthetically pleasing to look at.

I dunno what to make of this. ğŸ˜• I feel like they've exhausted certain story arcs & concepts. They should just move onto something else or go back to the first game's logic and keep it simple. They try too hard to explain everything when it's ok to leave things mysterious because of the classic Disney-magic system they use. We don't need to know in-depth details of how Pinnochio became a real boy or the nuances of the fairy godmother's power, or why mermaids exist. We can get by with simple surface-level information like what the first game offered. What we're here for is not to hear about the magic but to experience it.   I wanna go to cool worlds and see & do cool things. But the story is so lost and overly complicated now that I just feel tired whenever I see a cutscene -- which is so sad since they used to leave such a cool and powerful impact in the first game (and even in kh:com & kh2).  I think KH3 revealed to everyone undeniably that the writer(s) have written the story into a corner. And how many times is Sora gonna fall asleep or have his memories compromised? So it just seems like they're reusing the same ideas they used for the most popular games in the kingdom hearts series -- either to trigger nostalgia or make desperate attempts at recapturing the "magic" the series seems to have lost.  Overexplaining and making things too complicated for the majority of the audience is what took the magic away. If they can accept that, then maybe they can come up with some semblance of a solution that can save the series and put it back on track.
